After I have completed for you, O sons, this book, which is the last of medical science with its complement, and I have reached the end in it from its expositions and its declarations, it seemed good to me to complete it for you with this Treatise which is a part of operation, that is surgery with the hand.
Since operation with the hand is prostrate in our region and time utterly private: until perhaps the knowledge of it perished, and the trace of it was cut off: and there remained nothing from it except small descriptions in the books of the ancients, which hands changed: and error and hesitation befell them, until its intentions were closed and its force lengthened: It seemed good to me to revive it with the arrangement of this Treatise in it according to the way of exposition, declaration, and abbreviation: and to come with the forms of instruments of the Cautery, and the rest of the operative instruments: with it being done from the addition of declaration, and its proper execution.
The cause however for which a good craftsman of it with his hand is not found in our time is: because the art of medicine is long, and it is necessary for its author to exercise himself before that in the science of anatomy as Galen narrated, until he knows the joints of the limbs, and their forms, and their conjunction and separation, and has knowledge of the bones, nerves, muscles, and their number, and their egress, and veins pulsatile and quiet, and places of their exit.
And for that Hippocrates said that a name with a name is much, and with work it is little, and especially in the art of the hand.
We however already said of that in the introduction to this book.
For he who is not knowing what we said of anatomy, is not purged, but rather falls into error by which men are killed: just as I have seen many of those who are formed from this science and boast themselves of it without knowledge, and without experiment.
Which is because I saw a foolish physician dissect a scrofulous abscess on a woman's neck and he cut into some arteries in her neck; therefore the woman bled until she fell dead between his hands.
And I saw another physician who presumed to extract a stone from a man who was advanced in age, and the stone was large. He therefore arrived at him and extracted it with a piece of the bladder. Therefore the man died on the third day.
And I indeed had already been summoned to extract it; and I saw from the size of the stone and the condition of the weak man that he would die.
And I saw another physician who was receiving a fee from a certain Duke in our land for medicine; and it happened that a black eunuch who was with him suffered a fracture in his leg near the heel; and the physician hurried with his ignorance and bound the fracture over the wound with lint and bandages, and a tight constriction, and did not allow the wound to breathe.
Then he discharged him according to his wishes. Afterwards he dismissed him after several days and ordered him not to loosen the bandage; and it remained so until his leg and foot became abscessed and reached destruction.
I was therefore summoned to him; and I hurried to loosen the bandage; and there followed quietude, and he escaped from his pains.
However the corruption had already been confirmed in the limb and I was not able to restrain it.
Put therefore the corruption ceased to spread in the limb until it died.
And I saw another physician who perforated a cancerous abscess; and it became ulcerated afterwards until the malice of it was magnified with its master.
Which is because when cancer is pure from melancholic humor then it is not necessary to approach it with iron at all unless it is in a limb which can tolerate it so that the whole of it may be cut off.
And for that reason, O Sons, it is necessary for you to know that the operation with the hand is divided into two divisions: namely, the operation which is associated with health; and the operation with which there is danger in many conditions.
And I have already roused in every place of this book where the operation comes which is fraught with terror and fear.
Therefore it is necessary for you to be cautious about that and divide it so that foolish people do not find a way to speak and dishonor.
Therefore accept the measure with solicitude and protection, and your infirm patients with ease and firmness, and use the better way leading by God's grace to salvation and praiseworthy succession; and dismiss terrible ailments of difficult healing; and lift up your souls from that which makes you fear, so that hesitation may enter upon you in your faith and well-being.
For it is more enduring for your glory, and more sublime in this world, and lastly for your quantities.
For Galen has already said in some of his admonitions. Do not treat a bad ailment lest you be called a bad doctor.
But I have now divided this treatise according to three chapters.
Chapter One.
On cautery with fire, and cautery with sharp medicine, chaptered and ordered from the head to the feet, and forms of instruments and tools for cautery; and everything necessary in the operation.
Chapter Two.
On incision and perforation, phlebotomy and venesections, and wounds: and the extraction of arrows, and things similar to that; and wholly chaptered, ordered according to the forms of instruments.
Chapter Three.
On restoration, and dislocation, and the treatment of torsion, and things similar to that; chaptered, ordered from the head to the feet, and according to the forms of instruments.
But before I recall the operations with it, it is necessary to say what its qualities of benefits and harms are, and in which complexion it is exhibited.
Therefore I say that speech concerning the quality of cautery's benefit and its harm is a lengthy and subtle science and hidden secret.
Indeed, many wise men have spoken on this matter and disagreed; and it suffices me to speak a little from their words, fearing delay.
Therefore I say that cautery is applied universally to every complexion which has matter and is without matter, except for two complexions, which are a hot complexion without matter and a dry complexion without matter.
However in the hot and dry complexion with matter they disagreed. For some said that cautery is beneficial in it. And others said the opposite of that, namely that cautery is not suitable in illness which is from heat and dryness; because the nature of fire is heat; and it is unsuitable for something hot and dry to heal a hot and dry illness.
And he who says the opposite of that said: that benefit is done through cautery in every hot and dry illness which occurs in the bodies of men; because when you compare the body of a man and its humidities to the complexion of fire, you find the body of a man cold.
And I indeed say through his speech: because experience has already shown me that many times.
However it is not necessary for that to come about unless one who has already been proven and practiced in the ultimate exercise of cautery, and has known the diversity of complexions of men, and the disposition of illnesses within themselves, and their causes, and their accidents, and the space of time of them.
But there is no fear for you from the remaining complexions; and especially in cold and moist illnesses. For all physicians have now agreed upon them, and they did not disagree about cautery for them.
And know, sons, that from the secret of treatment by cautery with fire, and its goodness over cautery with a burning medicine, is because fire is simple, whose action does not reach except to the member that you are cauterizing; and it does not harm another joined member, except for slight harm.
But the action of burning medicine reaches that which extends from the members; and perhaps it causes illness of difficult healing to occur in the member, and perhaps it kills it.
But fire, on account of its subtlety and goodness of its substance, does not do that unless it overflows.
Indeed it has now become clear to us through experimentation, because of the length of service and study with the art, and standing upon the truth of things; and on account of that I excuse myself from the length of speech.
And if it were not because it is not permitted for this book of mine to bring to you the hidden secret in fire, and the quality of its operation in bodies in its expulsion, by which it expels illnesses through philosophical discourse demonstrated, which would agree with your minds.
And know, sons, that they themselves disagree on the time in which it is fitting to perform cautery, and they establish a better time for truth.
And I say that cautery is fitting at all times; because the harm that happens because of time is submerged in the benefit, which is attracted with cautery. And especially if the cautery is for pains from necessary pains, strong, urgent, which do not tolerate delay; because it is feared from them that a greater evil may happen, than a small harm entering because of time.
And let it not enter your minds, O sons, that which the common and foolish physicians do not esteem, namely that to the disease which is healed by cautery, there is not always a return; they suppose this consequence, but the matter is not as they think, because cautery is nothing but medicine applied in a place, which alters the complexion and dries up the humidities which are the causes of pain.
However, cautery surpasses medicine by the swiftness of its healing, and the power of its operation, and the vehemence of its dominion; and it is possible that the illness may return at some hour according to the complexion of the sick person, and the location of his illness, and its power: and that which is prepared in his body from an aggregation of superfluities therein, and which reaches him in its acquisition from foods, and things like them from causes, unless it becomes an illness in which cautery is administered.
Illness subtle in a limb of few superfluities and humidities, such as cautery of the tooth on account of pain and similar things to it, for it is possible that the pain will not return therein. But this happens rarely.
But truly the common saying again that cautery is the last of medicine is a right statement; not to what they intend therein, for they believe that there is no cure which agrees with medicine nor with another after the setting of the cautery.
The matter is on the contrary to that, and the intention that cautery is the last of medicine is not except when we administer modes of cure in some illnesses, and those medicines do not agree; then afterwards we administer cautery at the end of the matter, and it agrees; then from this it falls that cautery is the last of medicine, not according to the intention which the common people and many foolish physicians understand.
The ancients said that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron, and they did not say this except on account of the equality of gold and the exaltation of its substance; and they said that it does not make pus in the place of the cautery. But that is not absolutely true: for I myself have already proven it, and found that it does not do that in some bodies without others.
And a cautery with it is good, and better than with iron, as they said. However, when you make a cautery fire out of gold, it is not declared to you when it is ignited according to the amount you wish, because of the redness of the gold; and when cold rushes to it, and if you add fire on top of it, it melts in the fire, and turns into sheets.
Therefore the craftsman falls from it into occupation; and because of that a cautery with iron is made among us quicker and closer, out of straightness for the operation.
And I myself have now arranged this chapter on cautery, according to chapters; and I have arranged those things from the head down to the feet: so that it may relieve one seeking that which he wants from it.
Chapter II.
This cauterization applies to the dominion of humidity and coldness over the brain: which are two causes of headaches, and a multitude of flows of humors from the head to the parts of the eyes and ears, and a multitude of sleep, and toothache, and throat pain; and universally all illnesses, which happen from coldness, such as paralysis, and headaches, epilepsy, and apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
The method of cauterization is that you should advise the sick person: that he evacuate in the first place with medicinal purgatives cleansing the head for three nights, or four, according to what the strength of the sick person requires, and his age, and his habit.
Then advise him that he make his head bare with a razor. Then have him sit between your hands in a square way, so that he has already placed his hands upon his chest.
Then place the root of your palm upon the root of his nose between his eyes. Therefore wherever your middle finger shall arrive, mark that spot with a cautery.
Then a cautery with olive oil: which has this shape.
Then place it upon the spot marked with the cautery, with a downward motion, whereby your hand shall be gradually constricted, and you shall revolve it. Then quickly lift your hand and look at the spot.
And if you see that a quantity equal to the head of an awl or the size of rue has already been exposed from the bone, then lift your hand. And if not, repeat your hand with the same iron or with another if it becomes cold, until you see the bones which I told you.
Then take some salt and dissolve it in water, and imbibe the cotton in it, and place it upon the spot, and leave it for three days.
Then place cotton imbued with butter upon it, and leave it upon the spot until the burn is destroyed. Then care for it with tetrapharmakon ointment until it heals.
Now they have said that the more a wound remains open, the more pus it emits, therefore it is better and more beneficial.
And some of them have said that the skin should be cauterized down to the bone, and the cautery should be held until something of the thickness of bone is scorched.
Then after that which has been scorched is scraped from the bone, it shall then be cared for.
And others say that it is necessary with the cautery to reach the very end until it imprints a shape upon the bone so that the bone falls, which is done like the shape of a kirate: or an instrument which women put in with a small alphabet infused; and they consider that vapors of the head are exhaled from this place, and the wound is left open for a long time.
Then it should be cared for until it becomes consolidated.
But these two kinds of cautery do not seem to me to be anything other than according to the way of fear in certain people.
And it is better for me to dismiss him, with his health.
For the head is weakened by the breaking of its natural continuity, as we have testified in other members; and especially when the head of a weak and frail person is infirm; and indeed the first kind of cautery is safer and better for me, and I use it; therefore operate with it in safety.
Chapter III.
When a chronic pain occurs throughout the whole head and it is prolonged in a weak person, and they use leeches, cupping glasses, purgatives, oils, and poultices. And especially if it has already been cauterized with one cautery, which we have described, and nothing is conferred upon him from those things, then consider. For if the head of a weak person is strong by nature and is not frail, and it finds intense cold, then cauterize with another cautery under that one a little. Then cauterize him over the whole horn of his head with a cautery, so that it does not go through the skin, and uncover a quantity from the bone as we have described. And cauterize him with one cautery on the back of his head, in a place called the vas; and it is the place where windy currents are placed; and elevate your hand in this, and do not uncover the bone. For the weak person finds on account of that intense pain, and different from the pain of all the other head cauteries.
And I will say this cautery in its place; and it is necessary that it be a cautery with which the horns of the head are cauterized, and the back of his head with a more subtle cautery than that with which the middle of the head is cauterized.
Chapter IV.
When pain and swelling occur in a part of the head, or the pain extends as far as the eye, and the head is cleansed with purifying medicines, and the remaining treatment, which I have mentioned in the divisions of diseases, is administered, and that does not bring it all together: then cauterization is applied in this case according to two methods: either cauterization with a sharp burning medicinal agent; or with iron.
Cauterization, however, with a sharp burning medicinal agent is done as follows: you take one clove of garlic, and peel it, and cut off its ends from both sides. Then split the area of pain at a time when bloodletting is wide, until a place under the skin is made where the clove is gripped.
Therefore insert it just under the skin until it is concealed; then bind over it with a bandage of decent constriction and leave it for fifteen hours; then loosen it and remove the garlic, and let the wound rest for two or three days; afterwards apply a poultice soaked in butter over it until the place produces pus; then treat it with ointment until it heals.
And if you wish to do this with some burning medicines, which I have written about in the twelfth treatise, On Burning Medicines.
Cauterization of it with iron, however, is done in this way. Heat a cautery, which has this shape.
And it is called a Clavis because the shape of its head is like the shape of a key, in which there is a certain curve, and in the middle of it there is a small prominence.
Then place it upon the spot and hold your hand steady; and rotate the iron gradually with speed; and let the quantity that is cauterized be half the thickness of the skin. And raise your hand so that the artery below is not injured and blood flow occurs.
Then soak a swab in salt water and place it on the spot and leave it for three days; then put the swab with butter; afterwards treat with ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish, cauterize this hemicranium with the second blade end of the cautery. And beware of cutting an artery in this hemicranium, not an old one properly.
On the way of cauterizing an old hemicranium.
When you treat a hemicranium with what we said from the preceding treatment and what we said in the divisions of diseases, and the treatment does not take effect; and you see from the ailment that it is not sufficient for it what we said from the first cautery with medicine, or with fire cautery, then it is necessary to ignite the knife cautery until it whitens after you make a line on the place of pain, whose length is half a finger, or something like that; and place your hand with one finger, and squeeze it until you hit the artery and reach the mouth.
However it is necessary for you to be careful of the continuation of the jawbone which moves at mastication so that the side or the nerve which moves it is not injured, from which a spasm may occur.
And be careful and cautious about the flow of blood from the artery which has been cut. For there is fear in its cutting off, and especially for him who does not know what he is doing, and is not studious nor experienced; and he abandons the operation with it at first.
And I will come with a reminder of managing the flow of blood occurring from an artery according to its own way and in its place in this book.
If you see from the illness that this cautery is not enough for it, and you see a weak body tolerating the cautery in the middle of the head as we have described, care for the wound until it heals.
And if you wish, apply the cautery that we said in the chapter on extraction of an artery with a cautery having two knives. For this cauterization is better and more effective.
On the method of cauterizing for ear pain.
When ear pain occurs from cold and is treated with solutions and the remaining treatment as we said in the division, and the pain does not go away, then apply heat with a cautery; and it is that which is called a Point, its shape is this.
Then make points with it after igniting it around the entire ear, as it revolves: or around both if there is pain in both at the same time. And hold the cautery away from the root of the ear a little after you have marked the places with an ointment: and let the quantity of the cautery be ten points in each ear, and like that.
Then care for the places until they heal.
On the method of cauterizing for torture.
Chapter Seven.
The torture that is treated with cautery is not except for species that occur from phlegm, according to what we said in the divisions of diseases.
And avoid cautery for species that occurs from dryness and nerve spasm.
When you treat this species of torture with rue, purges and gargles, and your treatment does not work, then it is necessary for you to cauterize the weak person in three places: one at the root of the ear, and a second a little below its temple, and a third at the junction of the two lips.
And place your cautery opposite the weak part. For softening does not happen except in the part which appears healthy.
And the form of the cautery is that you cauterize with the cautery itself directly at the upper end of the ear under the horn of the head a little; and again at another time; the length of which should be according to the length of the thumb. And place your hand with the cautery until half the thickness of the skin is burned.
And this is the form of the cautery, and it is a kind of knife, whose form has been mentioned; however it is not thinner by a little, as you see; and it must be that the knife in it has a superfluous thickness a little.
Then treat the places with what precedes until they are healed.
On the method of cauterizing in old apoplexy.
When apoplexy becomes old, and you treat it with what we have said, and your medication does not work, and the patient does not have a fever, then cauterize him with four cauteries over all the horn of his head, and one cautery in the middle of the head, as we have said, and one cautery on the back of the head, according to what precedes; and let the method of cautery be according to what precedes.
Also, cauterize with a cautery over the mouth of the stomach; and this is the last resort.
Then treat it with what precedes.
Chapter Nine.
It is necessary that first, the sick person be given a large dose of hyssop in their drink, and pills to cleanse the brain.
Then shave the head of the sick person completely and place on the back of their head a plaster made of synaph, as described in the treatise on plasters; and apply it several times.
For indeed this is the method of cautery, and do that in the same order as I said there.
Therefore if it heals by that, it is good. If not, then make for him three cauteries on the back of his head, which are descending from the top of the head down to the lower part of the eye; and put a finger's breadth between each cautery.
Then take care of the cautery as with the one that preceded it.
But if you wish an addition, and he is weak enough to tolerate it, then make for him a cautery in the middle. But if you wish an addition, then cauterize it above the two horns.
Then take care of it until it heals, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to the form that has been given.
On the method of cauterizing in paralysis, and softening.
Chapter Ten.
It is necessary that you proceed in the purification of the head with lye and with what we have said.
Then shave the head of the sick person; afterwards cauterize it with a cautery in the middle of the head, and a cautery on each horn of the head, and a cautery on the back of it, and three on the vertebrae of the neck.
But if you are lacking in the illness softening of the body with those and he is weak enough to tolerate it, and the illness is strong; then cauterize him with four cauteries on the vertebrae of the back, and the last one with a cautery, until it burns out most of its skin, and raise your hand. Then take care of it until it heals; and thus let the cautery be olive-shaped.
On the method of cautery in epilepsy.
An epileptic person is not cauterized unless his epilepsy is from phlegm.
Therefore it is necessary that you cleanse his brain first with vinegar, and with the remaining treatment which we said in the division: when the patient is large, or he can tolerate the reception of medicines.
But if he is a child who cannot tolerate medicines, then a gargle and cleansing chews are administered for the brain, before that for many days with improvement of foods.
Then shave his head, afterwards cauterize it with one cautery in the middle of the head, according to what preceded in the manner; and with another cautery on the back of his head, and with a cautery over every horn of his own head. But if the patient is strong and can tolerate it, then cauterize him with the cauteries which I said in those having paralysis, and softening of the body over the vertebrae of the neck, and vertebrae of the back; and let the cautery be olive-oil according to the manner which preceded.
But if the patient is a child, then place a subtle cautery, according to this manner.
Concerning the manner of cauterizing in melancholy.
When the causes of melancholy are corrupted humors and thick phlegm, then cauterize him with the cauteries which we said in those having paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is a superfluity inclined toward melancholy and the body of the sick person is damp, then give him a drink that will cleanse his brain, according to what preceded in the division; then shave the head of the sick person, and afterwards make a decent headband from linen, like a circle.
Then place it in the middle of the head; and let the patient sitting straight be held on all sides.
Then present a liniment. And it is more fitting from old butter. And heat it over fire with a tempered heat measurement which the finger can tolerate when inserted into it. Then evacuate it in the middle of its head in a circle, and leave it until it becomes cold.
Do that to the weak one once a week, with the rest of its good regimen, until it is healed.
Or if you wish, cauterize it by making many small punctures in it, except for what you hold with the cautery: let there be a smell.
For this kind of cautery moistens the brain with quality.
Then put a swab soaked in butter or chicken fat on top of it.
On the way of cauterizing in descending water to the eye.
Chapter Thirteen.
When the beginning of water is declared to you in the eye through the signs that I mentioned in the division, then begin and drink the weak one, with what cleanses its head.
And keep it from all moisture, and make it sit in a bath, fasting for several days.
Then instruct him to shave his head, and cauterize it in the middle of his head. Then cauterize it above the two temples with two cauteries, if there is a beginning of descending water in both eyes at the same time: or from one side, if there is a beginning of water in one eye: and cut off with the cautery all the veins and arteries that are under the skin: and let the cautery be long in the breadth of the temples: and beware of the flow of blood.
For if you see anything coming from it, then cut it off immediately with whatever medicine is possible: and I will come with the wisdom that is in the extraction of arteries, and cutting them off, and caution against the flow of blood.
And sometimes it is cauterized on the neck, under the two bones, with two cauteries lastly produced.
On the way of cauterizing in old tears.
When tears from the eyes are old, persistent, and are upon the veins and arteries which are on the outer part of the head openly, it is verified that this is from cold, phlegmatic superfluities; then cauterize with the same cautery as I have described in the beginning for descending water, a cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries above the two temples, and two cauteries on the neck under the two bones. And if it does not yield with addition, then cauterize it on every side cautiously near the eye, above the extremity of the eyebrow with a small cautery.
Concerning the way of cauterizing for a foul smell of the nose.
When you treat it with what we said in the division, and the treatment does not succeed, then hurry and give in a drink three nights a decoction of lentils: then shave its head, and cauterize it with a medium cautery, with an olive-wood cautery. Then cauterize it with a small clove-wood cautery, two cauteries above the two eyebrows a little under the hairs.
And be careful of the artery so that you do not strike it.
And this is the shape of a clove-wood cautery.
Concerning the way of cauterizing for softening of an eyelid.
When an eyelid of the eye softens from illness or humidity, then cauterize the eyelid with one cautery, with this moon-shaped cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize it above the two eyebrows a little with two cauteries on every side, and they will be lengthened from the two temples: and let the length of the whole cautery be according to the lengths of the eyebrow: and do not end your hand with the cautery, rather according to the amount that the third eyelid is burnt.
On the way of cauterizing an eyelid when hairs turn inwards and sting the eye.
A cautery is of two types: either a cautery with fire, or a cautery with a burning medicine.
However, in a cautery with fire, advise the patient beforehand to let go of their hairs, if they are among those who remove them, until they grow long and equal. But if they sting him at their origin, then bind his eyes with a strip so that they do not move until they are born.
When they are therefore born and equal, then place the patient's head in your lap; then mark over the eyelid of their eyes with a cautery stick, a mark that is according to the shape of a myrtle leaf; and let the beginning of the mark be near the hairs.
Then place a swab dipped in albumin or psyllium mucilage over the eye.
Then apply the cautery with fire, which has this form.
Then cauterize over the shape that you marked gradually in many passes until the surface of the skin, which is like the shape of a myrtle leaf, is entirely burned properly.
And the sign of the health of your work is: that if you see the eyelid of the eye already contract and the hairs rise at the puncture of the eye.
Therefore raise your hand then and let him go for three days.
Then place a swab with butter on it until the scab is eradicated. Then care for him with ointment until he heals.
If any hair should return after an hour, and the eyelid becomes softened, then repeat the cautery on that place as you did first.
But if the hairs are below: then cauterize it until it is raised to its natural place; and equalize it so that the hairs do not prick the eye.
It is as if you instruct the sick person to let go of the hairs until they are prolonged and equalized. Make from paper or cloth the shape of a myrtle leaf.
Then take from known soap, and from quicklime not soaked one ounce each or thereabouts; then grind them together with good friction, and do it quickly so that it does not cool down. Then from the pan put it upon the paper which you made like the shape of a myrtle leaf, and place it upon the eyelid of one or both eyes. And place under the eye a cloth soaked in albuminous matter; and let the head of the sick person be in your lap.
And place your index finger upon the medicine, and press it for a short time. And you will move it whenever the sick person feels the bite of the medicine; because he finds its bite like fire.
Therefore while this continues that he finds the bite, then let go of the medicine and move it with your finger. When therefore the biting ceases, then remove the medicine and wash the eye with water.
And consider then if you see the eyelid rise as it rises in contraction with fire or with incision, it is good; and if not, then repeat upon it from the medicine upon the place where the medicine does not imprint and does not stain until your operation equals and the eye contracts.
Then place upon it a cloth with butter until the skin of the burn is removed. Then care for it with diaphinicon ointment or another until it heals.
And it is necessary for you during surgery to keep the last precaution so that something from the medicine does not fall into the eye.
But if the eyelid softens after a few days and something from the hairs fights into the eye, then repeat the medicine upon that place which softens from the eyelid itself, just as you did at first. Then care for it until it heals.
And this is the form of a myrtle leaf.
And know that the eyes of men are diversified in size and equality. Therefore let your consideration be according to that, and the way of straightness is not hidden from him who has a desire for this art.
Concerning the method of cauterizing a lacrimal fistula.
When you treat a fistula, as we said in the divisions of diseases, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary for you to cauterize it according to this method.
Instruct the sick person to place his head on your lap, and let a minister hold his head between his hands so that it does not move nor shake with his head.
Then place a cotton swab infused in egg white or in psyllium mucilage upon his eye; then with fire a cautery, the shape of which is this.
Let it be concave, like the shape of a vulture's feather quill from one end, with which the cautery is made; and if you wish it to penetrate to the other end, and if you wish it upward then try this way.
But truly this concave shape is better for your purpose.
Then press the fistula, if it is open, and extract the pus from it, and dry it; and if it is not open then open it and extract its pus.
Then place upon it the cautery which has been ignited very hot.
Hold your hand with it for a short time near the cautery by the eye, toward the side of the nose, so that your hand does not wander, or the weak one is agitated; and place the cautery in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
So if you reach at the beginning of your cautery up to the mouth, it will be well. And if not: then repeat the cautery once, or twice, if necessary with it; and let it go for three days.
Then put a poultice with butter, and care for it with a drying ointment until it heals.
And if forty days pass it and it does not heal: then put an acute corrosive medicine on it until the mouth is uncovered; and scrape it according to what comes in its chapter.
And there is another way of cautery for fistula, which some first said. Direct it to the place of the fistula and find it; then put a thin cautery into the fissure, that is, a thin cannula, whose form is this. And pour into it a quantity of a drachma of melted lead and hold your hand with the cannula in good retention, and do not move the weak one at all so that the molten lead does not run or reach its eye.
And it is necessary to put a poultice soaked in albumin, or in water on the eye of the weak one.
For lead burns the place of the fistula and heals it with a wonderful healing.
If the fistula is healed with what we said from cautery, and care, it is good. And if not, then it is necessary to administer the nasal foramen and reduce the fistula to the course of the nose according to what will come in its own place.
On the way of cauterizing in lip fissures.
Very often fissures occur in the lip which are called pili, and especially in the lips of children.
Therefore when you treat these fissures, as we said in the division of diseases, and treatment is ineffective, then apply a small knife cautery fire in this manner.
And let its concavity be according to the subtlety of the knife.
Then immediately place the ignited cautery upon the fissures themselves until the cautery reaches the depth of the fissures.
Then treat it with cerate until it heals.
Concerning the method of cauterizing a fistula of the mouth.
When an abscess occurs at the root of the gum or in the palate or in the roots of teeth, then it makes pus and bursts; afterwards it becomes chronic, and pus runs from it, and a fistula forms: then treat it, and if treatment is ineffective, you must apply a cautery fire according to the size that fits into the fistula. Then insert the ignited iron into the fistula opening and hold your hand steady until the ignited iron reaches its depth and end; do this once or twice.
Then treat it afterwards as we said about treatment until it is healed.
Therefore if the discharge of blood is cut off and it heals, it will be good. And if not, then it is necessary to open the area and remove the corrupt bone according to what comes in its chapter.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the gums and softened teeth.
When the gum softens because of moisture and teeth loosen, and you treat it with medication, and treatment is ineffective; then place the head of the infirm person in your lap.
Then a cautery by fire, of which the shape will come after this, so that you place the Cannula upon the tooth: and introduce into it the ignited Cautery quickly: and hold your hand for a short time, until the weak one feels the heat of the fire has now reached the root of the tooth.
Then raise your hand: then repeat the Cautery several times, according as you wish.
Then let the weak one fill his mouth with salt water, and hold it for one hour: and spit it out.
For the tooth loosened is made firm, and the softened gum is tightened, and the corrupted moisture is dried.
Concerning the way of cauterizing in toothache.
When toothache is because of coldness, or there is cold in it itself, or a worm, and healing does not come with medicine: then the Cautery is in itself according to two ways: either a Cautery with butter; or a Cautery with fire.
But the Cautery of it with butter is, that you take vaccinum butter, and boil it in an iron spoon, or in a brazier. Then take a cotton swab, and wrap it upon the extremity of the tentacle. Then immerse it in the boiled butter: and place it upon the aching tooth quickly, and hold it until it becomes cold: then repeat it several times, until the power of the fire reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, immerse wool, or cotton in cold butter, and place it upon the aching tooth: and put ignited iron upon it, until the fire reaches the depth of the cavity of the tooth.
But the cauterization of it with fire is, that you direct to an air cannula, or an iron cannula. And let there be something of thickness in its body, so that the sharpness of the fire does not reach the mouth of the weak one.
Then a cautery by fire, whose shape will come, and place it upon that tooth, and hold your hand until the cautery becomes cold.
Do that several times, for the pain will be removed, either on the same day or another day.
And it is necessary in the impression of that cautery, that the weak person fill his mouth with good butter, and hold it for an hour; then he spits it out.
And this is the form of the cautery.
Cauterize with whichever extremity you wish according to what is possible; and this is the form of the cannula.
On the manner of cauterizing in hernias.
When hernias are from phlegm, and from cold humors, and are not obedient to digestion by medicines, and you wish for their quick digestion; then a concave cautery by fire, whose form is this.
Having two open extremities, so that the smoke may exit at the cautery from one extremity; and place it ignited upon the hernia once, and a second time, if needed by it, until it reaches the depth of the hernia.
Which if the hernia is small; then place the cautery according to the amount of the hernia.
Then leave it for three days, and place upon it cotton infused in butter until what the fire burned is removed.
Then care for it with tooth ointment until the shape of the cannula is healed.
On the manner of cauterizing in hoarseness of voice and constriction of breath.
When humors overcome the canals of the lungs, and especially when it is with coldness of complexion, then it is necessary that the weak person be first evacuated with dissolving medicines.
Then cauterize it at night at the root of the throat in a depressed place; and be careful not to reach the throat with the cautery, nor into the skin, except a little bit of it.
Then cauterize it with another cautery at the junction of the neck in the last vertebra, ending it; and let the cautery be sharp according to the previous way.
Then treat it with what preceded until it is healed.
On the way of cauterizing in illnesses of the lung and cough.
When the cough and lung ailment are from cold humors, and the weak person does not have a fever, nor phthisis, and the ailment is old: then cauterize him with two cauteries above the collarbone in depressed, gentle, empty places. And with another cautery in the middle of the chest between the two nipples; and let the cautery be cannula-shaped according to the form that preceded.
And if you wish your cauterization to be by puncturing with a cautery, which is called a Punctum, whose shape preceded in the puncturing of ear pain: and let the punctures be from thirty punctures up to almost others.
Then treat him with what preceded until he is healed.
And now let the cautery have three branches according to this form. Therefore the cauterization is relieved when you do it with that juice and three cauteries together.
Chapter Twenty-Seven.
When the head of the humerus is dislocated because of humors, and it is not fixed within an hour of its return from its dislocation until it becomes accustomed to returning, then it is dislocated by a slight movement which happens as we have already testified: then it is necessary that you first reduce the dislocation. Then the weak person is laid on his back, or on his sound side. Then lift the skin which is inside the scrotum upwards with the fingers of your left hand: and if the joint dislocates inwards.
Then, having a burning cautery, apply two true points. Whose shape is this.
Then cauterize the skin until it penetrates to the other side, and the figure of the cautery will come with four cauteries.
And sometimes the cautery is done with a cautery having three points, so that the figure of the cautery then becomes six points: and the points are tested according to subtlety.
And this is the shape of a cautery having three points.
And sometimes one more is added in this way, so there are eight cauteries.
Then place bruised leeks with salt on the cautery. Then make the weak person adhere to tranquility so that the limb does not move for a while until it is strengthened.
And if the dislocation is upwards, and this rarely happens, then cauterize it yourself above the shoulder with a clavicle cautery, or by puncturing with many cauteries.
For the joint is strengthened and moisture is removed: and the weak person is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the stomach.
When cold and much moisture happen in the stomach until they draw it away from its own complexion, and catarrhs are multiplied to it, and there are frequent modes of treatment, and it does not help: then it is necessary for the weak person to be laid on his back, and to extend his legs and arms. Then cauterize with three cauteries, the cautery under the pectoral spoon the size of one finger with a clavicle cautery, and two cauteries below on both sides of one cautery, until the figure of the cauteries becomes triangular. And lengthen between each so they do not join together when they form pus.
And let the depth of the cautery be the quantity of two-thirds of the thickness of the skin.
And let the shape of the cauteries be according to this form without addition: and if you wish, cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form: and let the cautery with which this cautery is made be one according to the shape of a circle according to this form.
And the stomach is cauterized by pricking it for he who is frightened by this cautery: and it is that you make a sign upon the stomach a prick according to the quantity which you wish with an encaustic; then cauterize it itself with a point cautery; then care for it with the care which preceded until it is healed.
On the way of cauterizing a cold epar.
When it happens in the epar that pain arises from coldness and humidity, or from thick windiness, until superfluous egresses from its natural complexion, and the infirm is cured with that which we have said, and does not make progress in it: then it is necessary that the infirm lies on his back upon his neck, and makes three cauteries with an encaustic according to this figure, and the same quantity upon the epar below the hypochondria where the elbow of a man reaches; and let the space which is between each cautery be according to the thickness of a finger: and let the cautery be straight according to the length of the body: and do not press your hand hard with the cautery.
And let the quantity of that which is burned from the thickness of the skin be the quantity of half of it not added to; and let the infirm stand upon his own feet.
But if he is not standing, then let him lie down who has already extended his legs and raised his arms.
This is the form of a cautery.
And it is indeed possible for you, to cauterize with this cautery using a knife cautery, when you have subtlety and prudence in the art.
And beware that you do not proceed too far in cauterization, and the thickness of all the skin is hardened, wherefore the whole body is hardened, and it reaches to the intestines: for the skin there is delicate, therefore know this.
On the Method of Cauterizing Liver Abscesses.
When it happens that you wish to know if that abscess is in the flesh of the liver, or in its tunic: then if it is in the flesh of the liver, a weak pain and gravity without sharpness invade; and if it is in the tunic of the liver, with the pain there is vehement sharpness; and you see now that the treatment has wearied its physicians.
Therefore it is necessary that the weak person lie down on his neck. Then mark the location of the abscess with a hot iron; then ignite the cautery which resembles a ray. And this is its form. And cauterize with this cautery one time, until the whole skin is burned and reaches the siphac, until all the pus comes out; then treat it with treatment for ulcers, until it heals.
And it is not necessary that this species of cautery be used, except by one whose study in the art of medicine is prolonged; and through whose hands these illnesses run frequently with experiment: then let him dare to perform this kind of operation.
But truly I consider it better to leave it alone.
On the Method of Cauterizing in Pleuresy.
The ancients said that a cautery with the roots of aristolochia should be applied to cold pleuresy in this way. Take a single long root from the dried roots of aristolochia, which is found among them and is as thick as a finger. Then immerse it in oil and set it alight with fire. Then cauterize with a single cautery between the extension of the collarbone and the neck, and with two small cauteries under the jawbone on slight slopes towards the part that is below the beard.
And with two cauteries also between the fifth and sixth ribs on slight slopes towards the back; and with another cautery in the middle of the chest, and another above the stomach. And with three cauteries from the back: one between the two shoulder blades; and two cauteries from the two sides of the chest, below the cautery that is between the two shoulder blades.
And it is not necessary to press your hand with the cautery, rather let it be held openly on the skin smelling.
And some ancients have said that there are men who use a cautery made of iron similar to a spoke; they ignite it and insert it between the ribs until they reach the abscess with it, and pus flows out; as we said in the case of a liver abscess.
But there is danger in this perforation with a cautery because either the weak person dies immediately or a fistula forms in the place, which has no cure.
On the Method of Cauterizing the Spleen Chapter Thirty-Two.
When you treat spleen disease as we said in the treatment in the division of diseases, and your treatment does not work, then a cautery is used according to three methods, all of which are correct.
One of them is to make three or four cauteries in a line along the length of the spleen according to the figure of the liver cauteries, whose figure precedes this one.
And let there be between every cautery a quantity of the thickness of a finger, or more or less.
And let the manner of the cautery, which we said in the cautery of the liver, be equally so.
And do not press your hand with the cautery: and let the patient lie on his back.
And another method of cauterization is: to have the cautery with two points of fire, as we said in the chapter on dislocation of the shoulder; and raise the skin which is in the direction of the spleen, where the left elbow of the patient reaches; and let your elevation be such that you raise the skin according to the width of the body, so that the cauteries may fall according to the length of the body.
Then insert the two burning points deeply until you penetrate the skin on the other side; then withdraw the cautery; thus there will be four cauteries.
And if you wish, cauterize with another cautery having three points.
Then take care that the cautery after you have let it discharge pus for many days; for it is more convergent than any other which has preceded from healing.
On the Method of Cauterizing in Dropsy.
A cautery does not fall in dropsy, except on the legs properly.
When you treat a dropsy patient with the methods of treatment which we said in the division, and the treatment does not converge, then it is necessary that you cauterize him with four cauteries around the navel, and one cautery on the stomach, and another on the liver, and one on the spleen, and two cauteries behind the back between the vertebrae, and one in the direction of the chest, and another in the direction of the stomach; and let the quantity of the depth of the cautery be near the thickness of the skin.
Then leave the cautery open so that it discharges pus for a long time.
And do not withdraw the weak from treatment after cautery with him, for it is necessary that two intentions be joined to him, and healing will hasten to him with the help of God.
The form of the cautery with which the abdomen is cauterized should be a claw, as its shape preceded; and that with which the back is cauterized, should be olive-shaped, according to its preceding form.
On the method of cauterizing feet and legs.
When they swell up with dropsy and are filled with clear water, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot in the nocrati region, which is between the auricular and annular regions; and raise your hand with the cautery, and do not twist it; then raise your hand and do not rub it at all.
For the clear water will redden, and the cautery should be of this form.
Then make two cauteries on both legs, and let the cautery be made with the sharp end of the cautery; and let the cautery be made according to the length of the leg, one below the knee, and the other below it, around the middle of the leg; and make two cauteries on each thigh. Leave the cautery open without treatment for a long time so that some water reddens from it; then treat it with the rest that we have said.
On the method of cauterizing in ventral hernia.
Chapter XXXV.
When there is a ventral hernia from cold and humidity, until the retentive and digestive powers which are in the stomach and intestines weaken, and it is treated with methods of treatment and does not heal; and you see the weak patient tolerating cautery of abundant power, then cauterize him with a large cautery on his stomach, as previously mentioned in the cauterization of the stomach with a circular cautery, and four small cauteries around the navel with a claw-shaped small cautery; and a large cautery above the groin above the pubic bone, or two cauteries.
And if you see excessive moistures, and a weak patient enduring it, then cauterize it with a cautery over the comb, and with a cautery over the whole groin; and perhaps you will add two small cauteries on the stomach near the large one.
For it is a beneficial treatment, whose advantage does not stray.
Concerning the manner of cauterizing hemorrhoids.
Chapter Thirty-Six.
When there are many old hemorrhoids in the anus, or one, and they are from thick, cold humors, or corrupted humidities, and they are cured with what we said in the division, and the treatment does not take effect: then cauterize with three cauteries over the lower spinal bone of the back under the almeidati a little triangularly, and with a cautery under the navel as if with two fingers.
And if you think that his stomach is chilled and his food is not digested, and you see his face swelling, then cauterize him on the stomach with a large cautery, according to what preceded; and with a cautery over his liver, and another over his spleen, with a clauile cautery: and let the cautery be open for some time; then treat him until he is healed.
Chapter Thirty-Seven.
When you excise atheromas, then heat a cautery that resembles a rod. Then introduce the heated one into the excised atheroma; and guide your hand until the cautery reaches the opening of the vein from which blood flows: do this once, or twice.
If therefore there are many atheromas, then cauterize each one with a cautery according to what we have described. Then treat them with what is beneficial for them from ointments, until they are healed.
And if you cauterize it with a large cautery over the ligature, it is most effective for healing.
On the Method of Cauterizing a Fistula in Ano.
Chapter XXXVIII.
When the sick person does not submit to incision and the work which we have described in its place, and is terrified of it, perhaps he may be healed with a cautery.
Therefore, when it happens to someone that a fistula exists, and it is longstanding, pus flows from it, and corrupt humors. It is therefore more fitting that you should examine it with a subtle probe. Then ascertain the depth of it with the probe.
Then ignite a cautery, which is similar to a rod. Then insert the ignited [cautery] into the fistula itself and mark the quantity in which it entered.
And repeat the cautery upon it until all those corrupt bodies are burned, once, or twice, or three times, according to the quantity of your need.
And be careful of burning a nerve, if it is there, or a large vein; or if the fistula leads to the body of the bladder, or to the body of the intestine, then be careful of all these places.
And do not do this unless when the fistula is in a fleshy place, and you think that it is not penetrating.
Then care for the place until it heals.
But if the place is sealed, and materials are cut away from it, and it remains thus for a long time: then know that it has now been completely healed.
And if materials are not cut away from it, then know that it is penetrating, or there is a corrupt opening in its depth, or as if it were one of those [fistulas], the recollection of which will come in its place.
On the Method of Cauterizing the Kidneys.
When pain occurs in the kidneys from cold or thick windiness and weakens because of it a person's body, then it is necessary to cauterize him above the almethenem above the kidneys themselves with a cautery over all the kidney with a clauili cautery, of which remembrance precedes.
And perhaps we should cauterize him a second time on the very almeidatu itself. Therefore three lines will come. Therefore they will be more ultimate in benefit.
Concerning the way of cauterizing the bladder.
When weakness and softening occur in the bladder from cold and humidity so that the sick person does not retain urine, then cauterize him in the lower part of the penis above the bladder where pubic hairs begin, with a cautery from the right side of the penis and another from the left: and let the length of that cauterization be according to the quantity of a knuckle; and cauterize him with a lower back cautery, or two cauteries if necessary: and it should be as preceded by a clauile cautery.
Concerning the way of cauterizing the matrix.
When cold and humidity occur in the matrix and it is forbidden by it from impregnation, and its menses are corrupted, and their provocation is delayed, and pain occurs to her upon their arrival, then it is necessary that she be cauterized with three cauteries around the navel as we said in the cauterization of the bladder, and with a lower back cautery or two cauteries: and let the cautery be clauile.
Concerning the way of cauterizing the ankle in dislocation.
When mucous humidities pour down to the ankle joint and become the cause of its exit from its place: and the sign of this is that one leg is prolonged over the other when they are compared to each other, and a void place is found in it.
Therefore, it is necessary that you apply the weak cautery above the Anchae pixid in a circle similar to the cautery itself. After you mark with encausto in a circle around the pixid, as it rotates; so that the pixid itself falls in the middle of the circle.
But if this cautery is not present for you, then cauterize it with three cauteries, with a large olive cautery; and let the depth of the cautery be according to the quantity of the thickness of all the skin.
Then care for it until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing in sciatica.
When pain occurs in the Anchae pixid, and the cause of it is cold and humidity; and the sick person is treated with what we said in the division, and the treatment does not work, and it becomes chronic; then it is necessary to dissolve the sick person from thick humors with foul pills, or with artificial pills, and the like. Then cauterize him.
And the method of cautery in this is according to two methods: either cautery with burning medicines, or cautery with fire.
Cautery with fire is according to many methods.
One of which is that you cauterize above the Anchae pixid itself with three triangular cauteries, according to this form. And make their depth good, or bad. And let the space that is between each cautery be the thickness of a finger; and let the cautery be an olive one.
Sometimes, however, cautery is done in the middle above the head of the Anchae itself. Therefore there are four cauteries.
And if you wish to cauterize with a circle, whose shape precedes in the cauterization of a wide dislocation, make it one: so that it is a circle containing the whole dislocation.
And burn the thickness of all the skin.
This is the method of cautery in sciatica, when the pain adheres to the wide area itself and does not extend as far as the hip and leg.
But if it extends as far as the hip and leg, then cauterize it with two cauteries above the thigh, above the place to which the sufferer points there, in which there is pain, and your cautery above the calf four fingers toward the hairy side a little: and let the cautery be a knife-shaped one.
And let the depth of the cautery be according to the depth of the thickness of the skin.
But if the sufferer points out that the pain extends as far as near the toes, then cauterize it there where he points with a point cautery, three, or four, or more, if he needs it so.
And if he points out the pain to be below the knee towards the leg, then cauterize it there with one knife-shaped cautery.
And beware in all your cauterizations that you do not finish with the cautery so as to burn a nerve or a large artery, and thereby bring upon the sufferer evil harm or contraction through it.
And I myself have indeed already seen one and another, from those who cauterized above the calf, and finished in the cautery, and the leg swelled up until a tumor reached the foot, and it was perforated all through and corrupted altogether: then there followed rupture of the belly, and death after that.
But if the pain is in two parts at the same time, cauterize both according to this method.
And certain wise men have said in the cauterization of a wide area, of which this is the method of cautery. Make a speculum of iron, its diameter half a palm; and let it have at its opening according to the thickness of a fingertip, or a little less: and within that speculum let there be a third speculum.
And let the space that is between all the specula be by the amount of a thumb knot; and let the specula be open from two sides; and let their height be as a thumb knot, or two thumb knots; and make for them a handle of iron suitably fitted to the specula.
Then heat it in fire until it glows and projects sparks; then place it on a pitch plaster, the patient lying on their side with the healthy side down. Then cauterize him with three round cauteries in one go.
Then let them go for three days. Afterwards, apply a plaster with butter; and leave the wound open for many days. Then care for it with ointment until it heals.
Albucasis says, with this type of cautery, O son, we have rarely used it, because of the terror of its appearance; and therefore, because we have found few who would endure it.
Nevertheless, it is among the good cauteries for him who suffers it, and finds its place with it.
A cautery however, with healing medicines is such that you make two specula having a perforated handle into which descends the bar of its door from bronze, or iron, the length of a finger; whose height should be two thumb knots, or approximately so.
And let the space that is between each one be the thickness of a finger, and let them be open below and above; and let that which contains them to each other, according to this form.
Then place it on a pitch plaster, the patient lying on their healthy side. And press your hand firmly upon the broad pestle. Then pour between the two circles water that has been heated slightly with fire and hold it for the space of an hour: let the sick person endure its bite and its burning, for he will find the bite like fire until the bite is quieted.
Then raise your hand with the instrument and wash away the warm water from the whole pestle with fresh water; then let it sit for three days.
And place butter upon it until the blackness of the burn is removed; and let it sit for several days, and pus will flow from it. For it is the final step in healing.
Then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
But if the pain extends as far as the hip or leg: make for him a bath that contains water, according to what you did with the pestle equally.
And this is the method of warm water; and I have already written it in the treatise on the rectification of medicines. Take alkali and quicklime, each a part equal to the other; grind them both, and put them in a new jar, whose lower part has one small hole according to the quantity that the radius itself will enter: and place under the bottom of the jar another glazed jar: and pour over the alkali and lime fresh water, so that it submerges each by a finger; then press them with your hand with good compression: and let the jar sit until sharp water descends into the lower part of the glazed jar.
Then collect all that water and pour it over other lime; and strain until it is renewed.
For then it will be very strong and sharp, which is administered in many medical operations, and in the cauterizing of other members. Because it effects the operation of fire itself.
And among medicines are those with which they cauterize wounds, such as alum, and gum arabic, and lime mixed with soap, so that both are blended together.
And indeed Galen related a cure of some ancient man, by which he was healed of pain in the neck and sciatic vein; and he greatly praised it. And he said that it did not need any other cure, and that he was healed by a single draught, until he related that perhaps he had gone into a bath and came out of it already well.
And it is to be taken from green rue; and if green is not found, let the dry one be taken, fresh; and it is rubbed much with a little fat, and placed on the wound where there is pain, or leg, or thigh; and it is tied on and left for three hours, or for as long as the sick person feels the heat subside. Then let him enter a bath.
Therefore, when his body becomes warm, put him on a couch. For the pain subsides and he is healed.
And know that no one ought to use a cautery with these medicines except after evacuation of the body.
And Dioscorides, who also said this, that goat dung, when it is cauterized with it, causes it to contract; and a cautery is made in this way. Let wool be taken and soaked in old oil, and placed on the deep spot which is between the big toe and the next one, and which is closer to the ankle.
Then take dry goat dung and inflame it in fire until it becomes charcoal.
Then place it on the wool and leave it until it goes out. Then repeat that. Therefore do not cease to do this until the feeling reaches the middle of the leg and the pain subsides.
And this method of cautery is called vaccinum cautery.
On the Cauterization of Back Pain.
Sometimes pain occurs in the back from many causes, either from a fall, or a blow, or excessive evacuation, and similar things, from the infusion of cold and humid matter; and cautery indeed does not apply except in this single species, which is caused by the infusion of cold matter.
Therefore, after the evacuation of the sick person with fetid pills and the like, three lines should be made on the back where there is pain, according to the width of the almeidate itself; after which five cauteries or more are marked with an encausto in each line, according to the amount that comes from the tolerance of the sick person's strength; and cauterization should be done with a point cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize with three or four cauteries, with a middle-sized clauile cautery, according to this form.
On the Method of Cauterizing in the Onset of Kyphosis.
Very often this disease occurs in young children.
And the sign of its onset in boys is: that a constriction occurs upon him in breathing near the elevation and motion; and the youth in the last vertebra of the back and its nodes, which has already begun to protrude above the other vertebrae.
When therefore you see this, and wish to do it, then cauterize it with a circular cautery according to this form.
And let the cautery encompass all sides of the vertebra equally; and if you wish, cauterize around the vertebra with a point cautery two or three lines; and let the points be close to one another.
Then care for the place until it heals with what we have said.
And beware, that you do not apply a cautery to a hump which arises from spasm of a nerve.
On the method of cauterizing gout and pains in the joints.
When pains in the joints are from cold humors which flow to any member of the body, then when pains happen in the feet, it is customary for physicians to call that gout specifically.
Therefore, when gout of a cold cause is treated with methods of healing, and the pains are not removed, then a cautery removes them.
And it is to cauterize him after evacuation around the joint of the feet with many cauteries; and let the cautery be olive-wood.
And if it seems best to you to prick upon the face of the foot, then do so with a pointed cautery. But if the pains ascend as far as the knees, or other joints, and this often happens, then cauterize him upon the whole knee with three or four cauteries on every side, with the same olive-wood cautery.
But if more of these cauteries are necessary for you, then cauterize him. And do not submerge your hand with the cautery, rather let it be about the thickness of the skin only.
But if the pains ascend to the knees and back, then administer what we said from the cautery in its chapter.
But if the pains are only in the hands, then make punctures around the wrists as two lines revolve.
But if any pain remains in the fingers, then puncture them upon every knuckle, and upon the comb of the hand.
But if the pains ascend after days to the elbows or shoulders, then cauterize both on every side.
And do not discharge the weak from good regimen, from reception of medicines. For if good regimen is done, and phlegm is evacuated, he will be healed with the help of God by this cautery.
On the way of cauterizing in ruptures.
When a rupture occurs in the groin, and the intestine descends, or the omentum to the testicle, and it is beginning nearby: then it is necessary that you order the sick person to abstain from food on his day. And let him use laxatives, so that feces may descend from his belly.
Then let him sit between your hands upon his back; and order him to hold his breath until it comes out, or the omentum, or the intestine appears.
Then reduce it with your fingers, and mark with a cautery under the rupture upon the bone of the hip, with a sign whose end is like half a circle towards the upper part of the body.
Then apply the fire to the cautery, which has this shape, until it becomes white and projects sparks. Then reduce the intestine or omentum to its cavity. Then let a servant place his hand upon the spot so that the intestine does not come out; and you have now opened between the sick man's thighs, and placed a cushion beneath him, and a servant above his thighs, and another above his chest who holds his hands.
Then place the cautery upon the mark itself, with your hand holding the cautery upright. And hold it there until you reach the bone with it; or repeat it with another cautery if you have not reached the bone with the first one.
And carefully observe from the exit of the intestine during your cauterization, lest you burn it, and thereby cause great harm or death to the patient.
And know that when you do not achieve an opening with the cauterization, your operation is of no effect.
And it is necessary that the cautery for infants be delicate, according to their size.
Then care for it with other ointments until it is healed.
And let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is sealed.
And it is necessary that you provide him with nourishment for the length of his healing time, which soothes his stomach so that the intestines do not prolapse during straining and defecation.
Then when he wishes to rise after forty days, then apply a well-made bandage and let him wear it for another forty days.
And he should abstain from labor, overeating and drinking, and loud voices.
For when he follows this regimen, he will thus be healed completely.
And I will speak of the treatment of ruptures with an incision in its own chapter.
But when ruptures occur in the rest of the abdomen and are beginning, and you wish them not to increase, then cauterize his rupture with a round cautery according to its size; and let that which is cauterized be about one-third of it. Then care for it as we have said, and it will not increase.
And some first-mentioners have already said that a rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautery, according to this form.
After it is marked with a cautery, and a line is placed which is across its width on the upper side of the rupture, and another line below. And place your hand in the middle with a hooked cautery.
But a cautery is first easier and better.
Concerning the manner of cauterizing for pains due to a fall or a blow.
Chapter Forty-Eight.
When pain occurs in certain limbs from a fall or a blow and that pain persists for a long time, and treatment with medicines does not help it, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with a point cautery.
And let the cautery be of every member according to its size and its suitability and its weakness and its power and the location of the twist and the pain from it.
Therefore if it is healed by the first cautery, it is well. If not, then repeat the cautery upon it.
For it is customary for these pains to transfer from one limb to the one next to it. Therefore it is necessary that you pursue them with a cautery until the weak one is healed.
Concerning the manner of cauterizing for leprosy.
Lepers sometimes are greatly helped by cautery. And especially the type of leprosy which comes from putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy; therefore when you wish to cauterize it consider.
If then leprosy is beginning, and you have treated it with what we said in the division, and it does not descend, nor stand still: and you are afraid for the sick person, that corruption may spread over his whole complexion: then cauterize him on the head with five cauteries: one in the middle of the head known, and a second below it towards the forehead at the end of the hair, and two above the two horns, and one behind on the nape of the neck.
And lastly put your hand with the cautery for a short time on it until it makes a small impression, and the crusts separate from it: so that the expiration of gross vapors from it may be relieved; and also cauterize with the cautery the spleen itself according to what was said before.
But if leprosy is already spread over the sick person and appears manifestly: then it is necessary that you cauterize with these cauteries which we said on the head, and with a cautery on the extremity of the nose, and two cauteries on the two maxillas, and two cauteries on the vertebrae of the neck, and six on the vertebrae of the back, and one large one on the buttocks at the root of the tail and one above it, on the very buttock itself: and two on the ankles: namely, one on each ankle, and two on the knees: one on each knee, and two on the shoulders, and two on the elbows, and two on the tendernesses of his chest: and cauterize him on every joint, from the joints of the fingers of his hands and feet: and cauterize on every heel of his feet, and on the knuckles of his hands.
And be careful for yourself from the nerves which are above the last part of the heel so that you do not burn them.
And sometimes one should cauterize with a cautery on the bone of the chest, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
And know that the more you add cautery, the more benefit there is, and the more healing.
And know that a sick person does not find pain in cauterization, as healthy people do; because his body is already stunned.
And it is necessary that the cauteries be of size and suitability according to the limbs and joints; according to what preceded from the kinds of instruments.
Then care for the cautery with herb flour and honey, and other care, until it heals.
On the manner of cauterizing in a stupor.
When a limb is in a stupor and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters and does not heal, then cauterize the stupefied limb with cauteries, according to what its size or smallness deserves.
And let your cautery penetrate into the thickness of the skin a little. Then care for it with ointment until it heals.
And sometimes it is cauterized for a certain stupor that happens to the hand and foot, at the exits of the nerves which move them.
But let no one presume on that unless he is wise in the anatomy of limbs and the exit of the nerves moving the body.
Chapter LI.
When Albaras grows old and nothing from medical arts takes effect in it; then cauterize over it with a deep cautery for a short time, according to the amount of the skin's thickness until the whiteness is removed and its color is changed.
Then care for it with herb flour and lentils with rose oil, and leaves of arnoglossa, and dove blood, and swallow blood; let there be a portion from each: mix all these things and spread them on cloth and apply to the place until it heals.
On the Method of Cauterizing Cancer.
When cancer is beginning and you wish to stop it, then cauterize it with a circular cautery all around its circumference, as it revolves.
Wise men have said, however, that it should be cauterized with the final cautery in the middle.
However, that does not seem right to me, because I fear that it might ulcerate, and I have already seen that happen many times.
And it is more correct to cauterize it in its circumference with a circle, as we said, or with many cauteries.
On the Method of Cauterizing an Adubelate.
When someone has an adubelate and it is delayed in maturation, either because of excessive moisture causing it or because of the weakness of age, when he is old and with little blood, or because of the time and you wish to hasten the maturation of the adubelate, then cauterize around its circumference with many small cauteries puncturing. Then let it alone. For it will hasten in maturation.
But if you wish to perforate it with a cautery, then use a hot cautery which has this shape.
And place it in the middle of the adubelate until it penetrates the skin; and let the cautery be weaker than the one that follows so that the flow is relieved.
Then care for it until it heals.
On the Method of Cauterizing an Eating Sore.
Chapter Fifty-Four.
A corrosive is nothing but a corruption in a limb that moves about and eats it up; just as fire consumes dry wood.
Therefore, if you see a corrosive in a place that can tolerate a cautery with fire, then use many hot cauteries, small and large, according to what suits the place where the corrosive is.
Then cauterize it from every side until you eradicate all corruption and nothing at all remains within.
Then let it alone for three days, and put upon the cauterized places sulfur pounded with oil until all the scabs and all corruption are eradicated.
Then care for it with ointments that produce flesh.
Therefore if you see that after three days healthy flesh is born in which there is no corruption, it is good.
And if not, then repeat the cautery upon that which remains from the corrupt places.
And a corrosive medicine is sometimes applied with a sharp medicine. For it itself arises in the place of the cautery.
However, cautery with fire is of quicker healing, and I indeed already said cauterization of it with a sharp medicine in the division; therefore take it there when it is needed.
Concerning the manner of cauterizing warts and moles.
Chapter Fifty-Five.
Very often this illness occurs in the lower parts of the feet and it is a thick, filtered thing which injures the foot.
And indeed cautery on them is according to two methods: cautery with fire and cautery with hot water.
But as for cautery with fire, it should be a concave cautery like a vulture's feather made of iron according to the size which contains the wart on every side and have subtle edges.
Then place it ignited upon the wart. Then revolve the hand with the cautery around the wart until the cautery reaches the depth of the wart; and let it alone for three days until it begins to emit pus. Then plaster it with mullein leaves crushed with salt and let the plaster remain upon it at night. It itself will be eradicated from its roots.
Then care for the place with a flesh-generating ointment until it heals.
But if they are not inverted, and they often happen on the surface of the body, especially on the hands and feet; then apply a cautery to them with hot water: and it is necessary that you take a cannula from bronze, or iron, or from a vulture quill: and place it upon a coal, or an althelul. Then pour a small quantity of hot water into the cannula; hold your hand and revolve it with compression of your hand for a little while so that the edge of the cannula is imprinted in the root of the coal, and the hot water finds a way to the depths, to the root of the coal: and let the patient wait for a short time over the bite of the hot water for an hour.
Then dismiss him, for the coal will be eradicated with its roots.
Do this to them one by one until you come upon all that are from them in the body.
Then care for them after they are eradicated with what generates flesh from ointments.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in tremors.
